			<p>Hi Barry</p>
<p>A very well ‘written’ post.  I think your days of constructing are way behind you…I completely agree with all that you’ve said.</p>
<p>I would also like to add that posting ‘high quality’ content is a much better way to go than just making lots of posts…even though you are not charging your Reader any money to read the posts…they are spending their time…</p>
<p>..if you can keep their interest and give them something of value, which you manage nicely, then they will keep an eye on your blog and come back time after time.</p>
<p>I have no doubt you will reach the 100 comment milestone.</p>
<p>Happy Days!<br>
Cheers<br>
Steve</p>

			<div id="comment_title"><a href="?cid=1154" rel="external">John McNally</a><a href="?cid=1154" rel="external"><img style="float: left; margin-right: 10px; border: none; display:inline;" src="http://www.gravatar.com/avatar/8c3d96a9ceda38c40865dc3c5240cb68?rating=X&amp;default=identicon" alt="No Gravatar" width="40" height="40/"></a> on <a href="#comment-1154" title="">July 29th, 2010 at 9:47 am</a> 						</div>
			

			<p>Very interesting and useful, as always Barry. <img src="http://barry-wells.com/wp-includes/images/smilies/icon_cool.gif" alt="8)" class="wp-smiley"> </p>
<p>I have got in the habit of writing 250 word posts, and I’ve done it so often I struggle to go over 300 words. <img src="http://barry-wells.com/wp-includes/images/smilies/icon_sad.gif" alt=":-(" class="wp-smiley">  This could be a problem when I start to write 400/700 word articles. </p>
<p>My tip for new bloggers would be to aim for 400 words,that way you’re on the road to article writing. <img src="http://barry-wells.com/wp-includes/images/smilies/icon_wink.gif" alt=";-)" class="wp-smiley"> </p>
<p>My other tip for lazy people like me, is to write about a personal subject, which is just a matter of opinion. ‘Abbey Road by the Beatles is their best Album’ for example. No need to research that, just write what you feel. <img src="http://barry-wells.com/wp-includes/images/smilies/icon_smile.gif" alt=":-)" class="wp-smiley"> </p>

			<div id="comment_title">JasonSer.com from <a href="?cid=1213" rel="external">What's The Most Powerful Life Changing Inspirational Story Of Your Life?</a><a href="?cid=1213" rel="external"><img style="float: left; margin-right: 10px; border: none; display:inline;" src="http://www.gravatar.com/avatar/200512210dfee8dd05fd1eaf6f5c91c6?rating=X&amp;default=identicon" alt="No Gravatar" width="40" height="40/"></a> on <a href="#comment-1213" title="">August 1st, 2010 at 12:48 pm</a> 						</div>
			

			<p>Hi Barry,</p>
<p>Very Informative Post you Have Here. <img src="http://barry-wells.com/wp-includes/images/smilies/icon_smile.gif" alt=":)" class="wp-smiley"> </p>
<p>I love your idea of “constructing” a post. Which I believe will be a great way for new blogger to start a post that can provide more value that just personal ranting all the time. You see,  I am not really a research kind of guy, but our approach here is workable for a person like me. Thanks.</p>
<p>One advise I would like to add is the [Frequency Of Blog Post]. When I just started my blogging adventure, I originally plan to post everyday. But soon realize that is simply too taxing and unrealistic with my schedule. Then a friend pointed out to me that is better to leave a time gap between each post as it will allow my readers, if any to have time to comment and response to my post. </p>
<p>I quickly change my approach and make it a point to blog not more than 3 times a week and only post when I have something important to announce or can provide something of value to my readers. </p>
<p>Cheers<br>
Jason Ser<br>
P/S: About open office writer you mentioned, is it a free program? Where can I get it?</p>

			<p>Hi Barry,</p>
<p>Interesting and helpful article on constructing posts.</p>
<p>Typing it in the open office is a good idea which I should try. I usually correct my spelling before I press publish but once in a while a word gets missed and I have to correct it later.</p>
<p>As for the process you describe it is helpful too. </p>
<p>Researching the subject may be necessary even for an experienced blogger.</p>
<p>I would suggest just absorbing the information and then writing from what you internalized spontaneously.</p>
<p>Constructing it methodically and carefully piece by piece seems too structured to me but it may work for some people.</p>
<p>I’ve always found it best to just start typing something and that will get the creative juices going.</p>
<p>Thinking too much about the perfect structure and construction can potentially lead to staring at a blank page for a long time.</p>
<p>Vance<br>
<span class="cluv">Vance@Opt in List Squeeze Plugin´s last blog ..<a href="http://www.vancesova.com/build-your-opt-in-list-with-any-wp-theme-using-sqeeze-plugin.php">Build Your Opt In List With Any WP Theme Using Squeeze Plugin</a><span class="heart_tip_box"><img class="heart_tip 12543" alt="My ComLuv Profile" border="0" width="16" height="14" src="http://barry-wells.com/wp-content/plugins/commentluv/images/littleheartplus.gif"></span></span></p>

			<div id="comment_title">Andreas Spyrou from <a href="?cid=1356" rel="external">Free Online Marketing Tips</a><a href="?cid=1356" rel="external"><img style="float: left; margin-right: 10px; border: none; display:inline;" src="http://www.gravatar.com/avatar/e097b48b226156116f005df15c302bd1?rating=X&amp;default=identicon" alt="No Gravatar" width="40" height="40/"></a><br>Twitter: <a class="twitter-anywhere-user" href="http://twitter.com/andreas_spyrou" target="_blank">andreas_spyrou</a><br> on <a href="#comment-1356" title="">August 11th, 2010 at 8:03 pm</a> 						</div>
			

			<p>Hi Barry,</p>
<p>Very good points. I prefer writing a blog post as it comes to my mind and from my heart first without worrying about the SEO keywords. I can add them later wherever possible. Doing the opposite will get your a SEO blog post that only Google’s ‘robots’ can read.. <img src="http://barry-wells.com/wp-includes/images/smilies/icon_smile.gif" alt=":-)" class="wp-smiley">  Remember a blog post is for the humans and not for the search engines.</p>
<p>The plugins we are using for the 100 blog posts challenge are very good and can help us to get a good search engine ranking.</p>
<p>A very good plugin you can use to improve your ranking is called<br>
“All In SEO Pack”. You can download it for free here:<br>
<a href="http://wordpress.org/extend/plugins/all-in-one-seo-pack/">http://wordpress.org/extend/plugins/all-in-one-seo-pack/</a></p>
<p>If you use FireFox as your browser then you can install a “dictionary &amp; language addon” from <a href="https://addons.mozilla.org/en-US/firefox/language-tools/">https://addons.mozilla.org/en-US/firefox/language-tools/</a>  This will enable you to correct your spelling without the need to writing first your blog post in Microsoft Word, or OpenOffice.org Writer. You can do it directly from your browser!</p>
<p>I hope you like my tips.</p>
<p>Take care,<br>
Andreas</p>

			<p>Hi Barry<br>
An excellent piece. Most of all it may me give myself a slapped wrist for falling out of the habit of inserting key word phrases in my posts.<br>
Another useful tip I was given was to split my blogs up into 3 types:<br>
1) Insightful – let your readers know what’s going on inside your head so that they start to empathise with you.<br>
2) Content – provide content from stuff you’ve either researched or figured out yourself. I love being able to share stuff like when I changes the RAM in my PC and it worked!<br>
3) Product recommendations – this can include affiliate links. Use this sparingly and only on products you have checked out and are happy to recommend. Every time you use it you’re drinking from the well of goodwill you’ve built up with your readers. So remember to fill the well back up again.<br>
Thanks as well for your comment on my blog.<br>
Best regards<br>
Doug<br>

			<p>Thanks for sharing your insights, Barry. It definitely takes practice to craft a truly magnetic, sticky blog post. And with every new post they become better. Thanks for encouraging new bloggers. It’s true: everyone can use a little lift <img src="http://barry-wells.com/wp-includes/images/smilies/icon_smile.gif" alt=":)" class="wp-smiley"> </p>
<p>One invaluable tip that I learned was to focus on my natural skills and interests. It makes any task easier and more fun. In blogging, this has the added benefit of generally not needing to do research beforehand. The topics I blog about are already part of my mental landscape. The research phase is done organically as I’m following my interest in a topic. Then the idea for a blog post comes to me and I can just get straight to writing.</p>
<p>I feel this would work wonderfully for new as well as experienced bloggers. What do you think?</p>

<p>It’s good that you put your thoughts into your blog posts, it lets your readers get to know <b>You</b> which helps build trust and long term relationships. The trick is to try and use some keywords as well so as to feed the search engines.</p>
<p>Remember though Joelle your post may be found by search engines but as one of the tips above said, it is read by humans and that is where your thoughts and personality come into it.</p>
<p>When writing your post, write as you normally would then have a look at the subject and see if you can find some good keyword phrases to slip into it. </p>
<p>As long as you maintain the flow you’ll be able to please both the search engines and the readers that come as a result of them.</p>

			<div id="comment_title">Vivien from <a href="?cid=1406" rel="external">Internet Marketing</a><a href="?cid=1406" rel="external"><img style="float: left; margin-right: 10px; border: none; display:inline;" src="http://www.gravatar.com/avatar/f9b11426e91818c60e18a4ab82bed08d?rating=X&amp;default=identicon" alt="No Gravatar" width="40" height="40/"></a> on <a href="#comment-1406" title="">August 16th, 2010 at 9:15 am</a> 						</div>
			

			<p>Hi Barry</p>
<p>Thanks for the wonderful pointers in your article.  They are useful to all bloggers, whether beginners or experts.  What’s important to remember is the objective of why we are writing the blog in the first place.</p>
<p>Just to add on to your Google Keyword Tool, it would help in our Google ranking if we were to consider the keyword density of our articles.  SEO professionals suggest an average of 3% – 7% keyword density for relevant phrases.  In additional, it’s important for relevant keywords to appear in the first few paragraphs of our articles, and preferably within the first two sentences. </p>
<p>All the best in your online business!</p>
<p>Rgds<br>
Vivien<br>

			<p>Great article Barry,</p>
<p>Using the information already out there to create a post of your own is only smart.<br>
What you should do is credit the original creater of the content by linking to them like you would in a regular book, example: “Just like X said in his post ….”</p>
<p>That way you stay honest, show that you are doing the work of finding good information all over the net for your readers and you might even get a relationship going with the blogger you credited, all bloggers eagerly monitor their trackbacks and will be over joyed to see you linking to them (hopefully they will do the same for you!).<br>

		<li class="alt" id="comment-1478">
			<div id="comment_title"><a href="?cid=1478" rel="external">Andy Brown</a><a href="?cid=1478" rel="external"><img style="float: left; margin-right: 10px; border: none; display:inline;" src="http://www.gravatar.com/avatar/88521e607ae3e965201e44dee06b0a32?rating=X&amp;default=identicon" alt="No Gravatar" width="40" height="40/"></a><br>Twitter: <a class="twitter-anywhere-user" href="http://twitter.com/andybrownimr" target="_blank">andybrownimr</a><br> on <a href="#comment-1478" title="">August 21st, 2010 at 8:11 pm</a> 						</div>
			

			<p>Hi Barry,</p>
<p>Good solid advice.</p>
<p>All too often I see people blogging on topics unrelated to the subject matter to their blog, or being too broad in their topic. The keyword research is paramount and an area worth spending time on.</p>
<p>In fact the biggest mistake I see is marketers not paying close attention to their headline. In the same way I may write 25 different versions of a headline for a sales letter I believe the same amount of thought should go into composing the right title for a blog.</p>
<p>Marketers will only bother to click on your listing if the headline hits all the sweet spots and critically offers up a benefit for the reader.</p>
<p>How to do X easily and quickly in x minutes isn’t exactly an original headline but in many cases this will win over so many other headlines that don’t consider the blog from the readers point of view and why they should spend x amount of minutes reading it.</p>
<p>Once again thanks again for your blog post.</p>
<p>Kind Regards</p>
<p>Andy<br>

<div class="comment-childs chalt" id="comment-1508"><p><cite><a href="?cid=1508" rel="external">Barry</a><a href="?cid=1508" rel="external"><img style="float: left; margin-right: 10px; border: none; display:inline;" ' src="http://www.gravatar.com/avatar/9fa0baba954cd26f53b90e3230595b5b?rating=X&amp;default=identicon" alt="No Gravatar" width="40" height="40/"></a></cite> Reply:<br><small class="commentmetadata">August 25th, 2010 at 1:07 pm</small></p><p>Hi Tej, welcome to my blog and thank you for leaving a comment.</p>
<p>I’m glad that you liked the post and hope that you’ve been able to take something from it.</p>
<p>How can you stand out from the crowd? By giving your readers as much value as possible in a complete, and relevent, post. I wouldn’t write the same post as someone else has, unless you feel that the original post is incorrect or has important information missing.</p>
<p>John Lennon once said “If it’s already been done why do it again? Make something original of your own”</p>
<p>I hope that helps Tej, thanks again for your comment.</p>
